1. Summary 
This technical report was prepared by SGS Canada Inc. – Geostat (SGS Geostat) for Nevado 
Resources Corporation ("Nevado" or "Company") to support the disclosure of the mineral 
resources for the La Blache project ("Project"). The current NI 43-101 mineral resources for the 
Farrell-Taylor ("F-T") deposit stated in this report have been disclosed in the Company's May 23rd, 
2012 news release.  
 
The La Blache Property is divided into 3 mineral claim blocks, the 25 claims/14 km2 La Blache #1 
claim block, the 621 claims/341 km2 La Blache #2 claim block and the 81 claims/44.8 km2 Paradis 
claim block. The main Iron-Titanium-Vanadium oxides mineralization reported here is the Farrell-
Taylor deposit located entirely in the La Blache #1 claim block.  
 
Mr. Maxime Dupéré visited the Property on March 26 and 27, 2012 for a review of exploration 
methodology, sampling procedures, quality control procedures and to conduct an independent 
check sampling of mineralized drill core intervals selected from drill holes of the Farrell–Taylor 
deposit. 
 

1.1 Property Description and Location 

The La Blache property comprises 714 claims covering 394 km2 located 150 km north of Baie-
Comeau along Quebec's North Shore region and is also situated near Hydro-Quebec's Manic 3 and 
Outardes River Hydro-Québec Reservoirs.  To the author's knowledge and at the time of the writing 
of this report, the La Blache project is directly linked to the La Blache property. 
 

1.2 History 

Exploration in the sector of the La Blache property began in the 1950's with the discovery of iron 
and titanium mineralization. From the 1960's to the 1980's, aeromagnetic surveys mapping, surface 
sampling, assaying and metallurgical test work resulted in the discovery of several mineralized lenses. 
In the 1990's, metallurgical studies of the ilmenite mineralization were performed at the Hervieux-
Ouest occurrence near the La Blache property.  
 

1.3 Geology 

The La Blache property is located in the North Shore region of the province of Quebec, part of the 
Grenville Geological Province. The Grenville Province extends for more than 2,000 kilometres in 
length and skirts the North Shore of the St-Lawrence River. Its width varies from 300 kilometres to 
600 kilometres and forms the south east segment of the Canadian Shield. The Archean rocks of the 
Superior Province and the Proterozoic rocks of the Otish Basin are separated from the Grenville 
Province by the Grenville Front. The tectonic fabric of the Grenville is predominantly northwest-
southwest trending 
 
The Grenville consists of gneiss domes and basins with complex and irregular structural patterns, 
intrusive rocks of variable composition, from gabbros to alkaline rocks. The lithologies are divided 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 8 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

into three major units: the gneissic and intrusive rocks of varied composition of the Hulot Complex, 
intrusive rocks that include the east-west trending La Blache Anorthosite Complex, and late 
crosscutting gabbronorites, gabbros, diabasic gabbros, mangerites, granites and pegmatites The La 
Blache Anorthosite Complex is an almost ellipsoid batholith of 35 kilometres by 20 kilometres 
within intrusive rocks that extends for 100 kilometres by up to 20 kilometres.. The anorthosites are 
cut by granites and pegmatites varying from a few centimetres to several metres of multiple 
orientations. 
 
Four lenses of titaniferous magnetite (Hervieux-Ouest, Hervieux-Est, Schmoo Lake and East De La 
Blache) are present as tabular bodies that are aligned over a 17 kilometre long arc (RG2002-01) 
located at the center of the anorthosites. The lenses are almost parallel to the axis of the large 
antiform defined by the anorthosites that is slightly discordant with the lithologies 
 

1.4 Exploration 

The Nevado 2010-2011 diamond drilling campaign was preceded by prospecting, sampling and an 
airborne magnetic and electromagnetic geophysical survey that covered both La Blache #1 and #2 
claim blocks. This early work confirmed the presence and continuity of several massive and 
disseminated oxides occurrences across the entire length of the La Blache Anorthosite Complex.  
 

1.5 Drilling 

In 2010, Nevado secured the mining rights and completed exploration work as well as 9,700 m of 
exploration diamond drilling totalling 32 holes targeting the main mineralized Farrell-Taylor 
magnetite-ilmenite deposit. In 2011, Nevado drilled a total of 12,600 m mainly in the claim block #1 
over the Farrell-Taylor (6,850 m), Leduc-Farrell (1,800 m), Hervieux Est Extension (741 m), E. 
Girard Showing (234 m) and other areas (2,973 m).  
 

1.6 Sample Preparation, Security and Data Verification 

The individual sampled intervals of half-split core were inserted in tagged plastic bags, sealed and 
inserted in large nylon bags readied for shipment to the ALS Laboratory Group - ALS-Chemex 
facility in Val-d'Or, Quebec. ALS Chemex is a fully accredited laboratory under ISO 9001 and 
ISO/IEC 17025 standards. Blanks and duplicates were inserted in the sample stream on-site at every 
20 core samples. 
 
Nevado implemented the regular insertion of analytical blanks and the analysis of duplicate core 
samples in the sample series as part of their internal QA/QC protocol. A total of 226 analytical 
blanks were analyzed corresponding to 2.4% of the samples investigated during the 2011 exploration 
program. All of the 226 blanks analyzed returned values over the detection limit. All of the blanks 
also returned values 5 times and 10 times the detection limit. No significant changes or anomalous 
values for Fe2O3, TiO2 and V2O5 were observed. The QA/QC results are considered to be adequate. 
216 half core duplicate samples were selected from the drill holes completed during the 2011 
exploration program. No analytical bias was observed. It is SGS Geostat's opinion that the QA/QC 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 9 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

protocol and the insertion of control samples by Nevado are within industry standards. The data is 
of sufficient quality to support mineral resource estimation. 
 
Overall, the correlation of the Fe2O3 assay results shows a good relationship. No statistical bias was 
observed as only 0.9% difference was observed on the average grades. On the other hand, SGS 
observed significant differences in the assay results between TiO2 (2.2%) and vanadium (7.9%).  
 
The final database includes the drilling data from 2010 to 2011 compiled from the Nevado 
exploration programs. Although the sign test clearly showed a bias at a 95% confidence level with a 
7.9% difference in favor of the original vanadium results, SGS Geostat is in the opinion that the 
final drill hole database is adequate to support mineral resource estimation. 
 

1.7 Specific Gravity 

An average specific gravity of 4.6 g/cm3 was used to calculate tonnage from the volumetric estimates 
of the block model. The average specific gravity used is derived from 183 measurements taken from 
representative mineralized core samples from the 2010 and 2011 drilling period by the client. 
 

1.8 Metallurgical Testing 

In 2011, Neomet Technologies Inc. (Neomet) of Dorval, Quebec, completed a first stage of 
metallurgical testing on the Farrell-Taylor massive oxides mineralization. Neomet adapted their 
proprietary process for extraction of all valuable metals from the massive oxide mineralizations. 
 
Preliminary metallurgical testing of the oxide mineralizations by Neomet indicated 90% recovery of 
Iron and 95% recovery of Vanadium into a final high-purity product. Neomet demonstrated that 
Titanium could be 100% recovered from the leach solution into a TiO2 (titanium-dioxide) product 
suitable for further processing to pigment-grade TiO2. Ammonium metavanadate (AMV), the 
precursor to V2O5 (Vanadium Pentoxide), was recovered from the leach solution at a purity of 
99.9%. 
 
Nevado plans to use Neomet's unique proprietary acid recovery and regeneration process, which 
operates at a fraction of the cost compared with more conventional and energy-consuming 
technologies such as pyrohydrolysis, especially when the latter is coupled with solvent extraction for 
Iron and/or Titanium. Simultaneously, the Neomet process produces higher-grade ilmenite of 
greater than 99% purity (TiO2), which is a premium product suitable for the pigment market or for 
processing into higher-quality steels. 
 

1.9 TiO2 Equivalent grade 

SGS Geostat introduced a Titanium Equivalent calculated variable into the deposit estimation.  Mr. 
Mike Curtis of Nevado provided price lists of the Vanadium, Iron and Titanium as of April 29th, 
2012. SGS Geostat did not do an extensive research of the dollar value of vanadium, TiO2 and iron

concentrates. A validation of the commodity prices was done from available public information and 
from available information from similar Projects.

 Titanium Equivalent Grade Equation:  
 
TiO2 Eq (%) = TiO2 + ((Fe2O3*0.62*120) / (1*2500)) + ((V*1.7852*0.0001*1*13500) / (1*2500)) 
TiO2 Eq (%) = TiO2 (%) + (V (ppm)*1.7852*0.0001*5.4) + (Fe2O3 (%)*0.033) 
 
Where V2O5 (%) = V (ppm)*1.7852*0.0001

confidential report 
 

1.10 Mineral Resources 

The mineral resource block model has been interpolated from 1.5 m long analytical composite data 
constrained within a 3D wireframe envelop of the mineralized massive iron oxides defined from drill 
hole geological interpretation. The mineral resource model is defined by block 10 m (east-west) by 
10 m (north-south) by 10 m (elevation) in size, located below the bedrock/overburden interface. 
The deposit covers over 1150 m on the ENE direction with an average width of 470m. The deposit 
widens at depth from 200 m on the WSW to approximately 715 m to the ENE. The deposit is 
slowly dipping at 20° towards the ENE and reaches a maximal depth of 600 m below surface. The 
average thickness is 50 m with a minimum of 15 m and a maximum of 85 m in the deeper portion of 
the deposit. The interpolation of the block grade was performed by inverse squared distance in 
multiple passes using anisotropic search ellipsoids increasing in size from one pass to another. The 
final mineral resources correspond to the estimated blocks located below the bedrock/overburden 
interface within the modeled envelop. An average specific gravity of 4.6 g/cm3 was used to calculate 
the final tonnage of the mineral resources based on the volumetric estimates of the block model. 
Currently, there are no measured resources and no indicated resources.  
 

The resources reported in this document are compliant with standards as outlined in the National 
Instrument 43-101. These resources were calculated using a minimum cut-off grade of 5.1% TiO2Eq 
and are amounting to 101,700,000 tonnes inferred category at 21.75% TiO2 Eq from a head grade of 
41.76% Fe, 18% TiO2, 0.18% V (0.33 % V2O5). 
 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 11 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

1.11 Conclusions 

The resources reported in this document are compliant with standards as outlined in the National 
Instrument 43-101. These resources were calculated using a minimum cut-off grade of 5.1% TiO2Eq 
and are amounting to 101,700,000 tonnes inferred category at 21.75% TiO2 Eq from a head grade 
of 41.76% Fe, 18% TiO2, 0.18% V (0.33 % V2O5). 
  
The Farrell-Taylor deposit contains enough resources to justify additional work on the La Blache 
property that could lead to a preliminary economic assessment study. 
 
The independent sampling done by SGS Geostat revealed that the average grade of original assays 
for the vanadium (V2O5) is 7% higher than the independent samples. It shows a bias at a 95% 
confidence level for vanadium (V2O5). SGS Geostat recommends sending duplicate samples to two 
different laboratories in order to determine correction factors. SGS Geostat recommends also 
continuing the QA/QC protocol. 
 
The Project needs more definition diamond drilling before being ready for any mining operation; 
this can be realized with surface drilling.  
 

1.12 Recommendations 

SGS Geostat recommends additional infill drilling on the Farrell-Taylor deposit for classification 
upgrade as well as the continuation of detailed cartography, and exploration work of known and 
future mineralized occurrences throughout the La Blache property. A conceptual cost of CA$ 
3,191,000 is estimated for the exploration.  
 
SGS Geostat recommends carrying out downhole survey measurements (dip, direction of surveyed 
holes) and the implementation of core orientation surveys on relevant 2010-2011 drill holes and on 
all selected future drill targets.  
 
Although there is no analytical bias encountered on the Nevado duplicate core analysis SGS Geostat 
recommends sending the core duplicates to a second certified laboratory in order to establish if there 
is a significant error from one laboratory to another. This suggestion is in line with the finding of the 
Data Verification section.  
 
The 7.9% difference for the vanadium and the 2.2% difference for TiO2 between original (ALS) and 
check sample (SGS Lakefield) results for vanadium may be considered acceptable however; SGS 
Geostat strongly recommends addressing the matter by sending duplicate samples to two different 
laboratories in order to determine the bias. SGS Geostat recommends also continuing the QA/QC 
protocol by adding reference materials (standards) that match the general composition of the 
mineral deposits of the area. SGS Geostat also recommends sending sufficient material from the 
Farrell-Taylor or other known similar occurrences and showings to a certified laboratory in order to 
produce sufficient homemade and certified reference material (standards). 
 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 12 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

Additionally, SGS Geostat recommends sending reference materials (standards) to the same two 
different laboratories for the verification/evaluation of these results and to have a better 
understanding of the bias observed for the vanadium and TiO2. 
 
Finally, SGS Geostat recommends to fine tune the Neomet Process.

2. Introduction  

2.1 General 

This technical report was prepared by SGS Canada Inc. – Geostat ("SGS Geostat") for Nevado 
Resources Corporation ("Nevado" or "Company") to support the disclosure of the mineral 
resources for the La Blache project ("Project" or "Property") located in the La Blache Property. The 
current National Instrument ("NI") 43-101 mineral resources for the Farrell-Taylor ("FT") deposit 
stated in this report have been disclosed in the Company's May 23rd, 2012 news release.  
 
The property (Figure 4-2) is divided into 3 mineral claim blocks, the 25 claims/14 km2 La Blache #1 
claim block (Figure 4-3), the 621 claims/341 km2 La Blache #2 claim block (Figure 4-4) and the 81 
claims/44.8 km2 Paradis claim block (Figure 4-5). The main Iron-Titanium-Vanadium oxides 
mineralization reported here is the Farrell-Taylor deposit located entirely within the La Blache #1 
claim block.  
 
This report was prepared following the guidelines set in NI 43-101 and the norm 43-101F1 
Standards of Disclosure for Mineral Projects. This report brings together all of the historic 
geological information from the Project and surrounding area. The bulk of the information was 
derived from the Ministère des Ressources Naturelles et de la Faune (Québec) ("MRNFQ") 
SIGEOM database and relevant information provided by the Company  
 
This report describes the basis and methodology used for the modeling and the estimation of the 
mineral resources for the Farrell-Taylor deposit drilling data collected by Nevado. This report also 
presents a full review of the history, geology, sample preparation and analysis, data verification, 
mining and metallurgical testing of the Project and provides recommendations for future work. 
 
SGS Geostat was commissioned by Nevado on March 1st, 2012 to prepare an independent estimate 
of the updated mineral resources of the Farrell-Taylor deposit from an open pit and hydrometallurgy 
processing perspective. Nevado supplied electronic format data from which SGS Geostat generated 
and validated a final updated database. 
 
Mr. Maxime Dupéré, P.Geo. visited the Property on March 26 and 27, 2012 for a review of 
exploration methodology, sampling procedures, quality control procedures and to conduct an 
independent check sampling of mineralized drill core intervals selected from drill holes of the 
Farrell–Taylor deposit.

2.4 Disclaimer 

It should be understood that the mineral resources which are not mineral reserves do not have 
demonstrated economic viability. The mineral resources presented in this Technical Report are 
estimates based on available sampling and on assumptions and parameters available to the author. 
The comments in this Technical Report reflect the author's and SGS Canada Inc. – Geostat's best 
judgement in light of the information available. During the mineral resource estimation process, 
different assumptions were made. These assumptions were used in order to calculate modelling cut-
off grades and resources cut-off grades following the "reasonable prospect for economic extraction" 
stated by the NI 43-101 regulation. There were no optimised pit shell (Whittle pit) done by either 
the author or the Company.

4. Property Description and Location 

4.1 Location 

The La Blache property (the Property) covers 714 claims for 394 km2 located 150 km north of Baie-
Comeau along Quebec's North Shore region and is also situated near Hydro-Quebec's Manic 3 and 
Outardes River Hydro-electric Reservoirs (Figure 4-1) To the author's knowledge and at the time of 
the writing of this report, the La Blache project is directly linked to the La Blache property. 
 
The Property (Figure 4-2) is divided into 3 mineral claim blocks, the 25 claims/14 km2 La Blache #1 
claim block (Figure 4-3) , the 621 claims/341 km2 La Blache #2 claim block (Figure 4-4) and the 81 
claims/44.8 km2 Paradis claim block (Figure 4-5). The main Iron-Titanium-Vanadium oxide 
mineralization reported here is the Farrell-Taylor deposit located entirely within the La Blache #1 
claim block. 
 
The Property has not been legally surveyed. The boundary of each claim block was defined using the 
MRNFQ website at www.mrnfp.gouv.qc.ca/mines/index.jsp, and the MRNFQ's GESTIM claim 
management system. 
 
All claims are active and in good standing. On the La Blache #1 claim block, all 25 claims have 
renewal dates of October 25, 2012. On the La Blache #2 claim block, the closest renewal dates are 
January 17, 2012 for a total of 320 claims. A renewal demand was made by Nevado and Tne 
MRNFQ response is pending. On the Paradis claim block, the closest renewal dates are March, 19, 
2014 for a total of 80 claims.   
 
Should any future application be made for a mining lease(s) on this Project, it would be possible to 
obtain all necessary surface rights and permits from the MRNFQ. Details on claims renewals, work 
credits, claim access rights, allowable exploration, development and mining works, and site 
rehabilitation are summarized in the Mining Act of Quebec that can be accessed via the MRNFQ 
website at: 
http://www2.publicationsduquebec.gouv.qc.ca/dynamicSearch/telecharge.php?type=2&file=%2F
%2FM_13_1%2FM13_1_A.htm or from the Canadian Legal Information Institute website at: 
http://www.canlii.org/qc/laws/sta/m-13.1/20080818/whole.html. 
 

4.2 Ownership 

As of May 14, 2012, the La Blache project (the "Project" or the "Property") covers 714 claims for 
394 km2 located 150 km north of Baie-Comeau along Quebec's North Shore region and is also 
situated near Hydro-Quebec's Manic 3 and Outardes River Hydro-Quebec Reservoirs (Figure 4-1).   
The Property (Figure 4-2) is divided into 3 mineral claim blocks, the 25 claims/14 km2 La Blache #1 
claim block (Figure 4-3) , the 621 claims/341 km2 La Blache #2 claim block (Figure 4-4) and the 81 
claims/44.8 km2 Paradis claim block (Figure 4-5). The main Iron-Titanium-Vanadium oxide 
mineralization reported here is the Farrell-Taylor deposit located entirely within the La Blache #1 
claim block. All claims composing the Project are map-designated cells referred as CDC. The 
Project is subject to ancestral rights as described in section 4.5.  All of the claims purchasing 
agreements are summarized in the next section.

4.3 Royalties and Agreements 

Nevado entered into an initial agreement dated December 30, 2009, to purchase the 25 claims - La 
Blache #1 Claim Block (Figure4-6) from Bertrand Brassard (the Vendor) based on terms set out in a 
Letter of Intent dated November 11, 2009, as part of a Qualifying Transaction  (the Qualifying 
Transaction) to list Nevado on the TSX Venture Exchange. Nevado paid $3,000 in cash and issued 
500,000 common shares at a deemed value of $0.10 per share. In addition, Nevado offered a 2% 
Net Smelter Return ("NSR") Royalty to the Vendor of which 1% could be purchased for a sum of 
$1,000,000.  
 
Nevado entered in to a second agreement also dated December 30, 2009, to purchase the 531 claims 
- La Blache #2 Claim Block (Figure4-6) from Bertrand Brassard, Guy Girard and Louis-Philippe 
Séguin (the Vendors) based on terms set out in a Letter of Intent dated November 11, 2009.  Also 
part of the Qualifying Transaction, Nevado reimbursed the sum of $30,000 divided between the 
Vendors and offered a 2% NSR of which 1% could be purchased for a sum of $1,000,000.  Finally  
an assumption of debt for a maximum of $60,000 related to the La Blache #2 Claim Block; and the 
issuance of 1,000,000 Common Shares at a deemed value of $0.10 per share divided between the 
Vendors. 
 
A number of the claims from the La Blache #2 claim block were abandoned in early 2012, followed 
by a purchase of 81 claims forming the Paradis claim block.. Nevado paid $10,000 in cash to the 
owner with no additional encumbrances. At of the writing of this report, Nevado and the owner 
were in the process of title ownership transfer of the Paradis claim block to the Ministère des 
Resources Naturelles du Québec. 
 
The authors assume that the documents, reports and other data listed are substantially accurate and 
complete in all material aspects. The authors have reviewed the mining titles (claims), their status, 
the legal agreement and technical data supplied by the Company, and any public sources of relevant 
technical information.  
 

4.4  Permits and Environmental Liabilities 

Nevado is conducting exploration work under valid permits delivered by the MRNFQ. There are no 
other environmental liabilities pertaining to the Project according to Nevado management. 
 

4.5 Ancestral Territory  

The Lac La Blache sector is subject to ancestral rights claims of the Innu of Pessamit, as it is part of 
the Nitassinan Ancestral Territory of Pessamit. The authors are not aware of any exploration 
agreements between Nevado and the Innu community. 
 
The Pessamit territory, which is near Nevado's La Blache property, covers an area of 135,000 km2 
and includes 4,000 members of the Innu Nation.

5. Accessibility, Climate, Local Resources, Infrastructure, 
Physiography   

The surrounding area is uninhabited. The nearest city is Baie-Comeau which is located 150 km to 
the southeast on the North Shore of the St. Lawrence River. The main employer is the Alcoa 
Aluminium Plant. The economic and industrial development in the region is based on mineral, 
forest and hydroelectric resources. There is a seaport at Baie-Comeau that facilitates the transport of 
ore or any other goods.  
 
Forest activities are very present in the region. There are substantial hydroelectric facilities. The 
Manicouagan region is situated at the intersection of Highways #138 and #389. Provincial Highway 
#138 links Montreal and Natashquan and follows the north shore of the St. Lawrence River. 
Highway #389 provides access to the mining towns of the northeast and links Baie-Comeau to the 
Labrador border. 
 
The climate along the west coast of the northern part of St. Lawrence River is one of contrast: The 
summers are short, warm (average of 14.5° C in July) and humid with frequent rain. Winters are long 
and difficult with much snow and strong winds. The average temperature is minus 25°C. Mineral 
exploration of all types including drilling can be done throughout the year on the La Blache 
property.  It is easier when moving heavy equipment in winter across frozen lakes and rivers with 
less damage to the land surface.  
 
Much of the La Blache property area has been burnt by forest fires at different times and lacks the 
normal woodcutting activities and secondary roads. 
 

5.1 Physiography 

The topography of the area is generally moderate to strongly mountainous. The land drainage 
patterns flow southward by small and large rivers. Outcrops occur frequently throughout the 
Property. The overburden consists of glacial-fluvial till and lacustrine deposits and is generally less 
than 15 m thick with an average of 3 m. Elevation in the area averages 525 m above sea level.  
 
Vegetation of the surrounding area is characterized by the boreal forest consisting of spruce, pines,   
poplars and aspens. Much of the La Blache property area has been burnt by forest fires at different 
times and lacks the normal woodcutting activities and secondary roads. 
   

5.2 Accessibility 

The Nevado property is located 150 km northwest of the city of Baie-Comeau. The Property is 
accessible via a forestry gravel road to the nearby forestry camp Boisaco, approximately 15 km 
southwest of the Farrell-Taylor drill holes. There is no electricity on site.  The forest activities are 
very lively in the region except at Farrell-Taylor where a major forest fires burnt all available 
economic lumber wood. The Manicouagan region is situated at the intersection of Highways #138 
and #389. Provincial Highway #138 links Montreal and Natashquan and follows the north shore of 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 38 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

the St. Lawrence River. Highway #389 provides access to the mining towns of the northeast and 
links Baie-Comeau to the Labrador border. 
 

5.3 Climate 

The climatic data used to characterize the sector under study comes from the meteorological station 
of Baie-Comeau Airport and is available at the National Climate Data and Information Archive at 
www.climate.weatheroffice.gc.ca. These observations were carried out from 1971 to 2000. 
Exploration work in the area can typically be carried out year-round but occasional soft ground in 
the areas covered by wetlands could create difficult working conditions from late spring until early 
winter. 
 
In the Cote Nord region, the average daily temperature is slightly above the freezing point, i.e. 1.5°C. 
The average temperature during July reaches 15.6°C, while the temperature in January falls to -15°C. 
  
Annual precipitation totals 684.1 mm of water annually in the area. Average monthly precipitation 
ranges from 11.4 mm in February to 92.1 mm in September. Snow falls from October to April, but 
is much more significant from November to March. The year average snow fall is 681.4 mm.  
 
The anemometric data between 1971 and 2000 indicates that from June to October the SW winds 
are dominant whereas from February to May, the W-NW to E winds are more frequent. In this 
sector, the winds have an average velocity of 13.6 km/h, ranging from 13.3 to 17.6 km/h. 
 

5.4 Local Resources and Infrastructures 

The regional resources regarding labour force, supplies and equipment are sufficient, the area being 
well served by geological and mining service firms mostly concentrated in the Sept-Iles-Port Cartier 
area and in Labrador City, Labrador. The city of Baie-Comeau, with more than 30,000 inhabitants, is 
one of the cities of the Cote-Nord region and has the necessary infrastructures and workforce to 
support a mining operation.  While there is currently a general shortage of qualified personnel in the 
mining and exploration sector, the location of the Project is favourable in that regard.  The main 
employer in Baie-Comeau is the Alcoa Aluminum Plant. The economic and industrial development 
in the region is based on mineral, forest and hydroelectric resources. The area is served by the 
shipping port of Baie-Comeau, which is navigable all year and handles alumina and other trades. All 
major services are available in Baie-Comeau.  
 
The fauna and flora in the region are typical of the boreal forest. Coniferous trees dominated by 
sparse spruce cover the La Blache area. Other tree species like balsam fir, larch and pine, as well as 
clumps of broadleaved birch, poplar, willow, alder and mountain ash, are also found. The local 
forest is home to about forty species of mammals, including wolves, lynxes, foxes, bears and moose. 
Ducks, Canada geese, snow geese, snowy owls, eagles, falcons, ptarmigans and loons are among the 
bird life of the region. The aquatic fauna is mainly represented by lake trouts, walleyes, brook trouts 
and pikes.

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

6. History 
Exploration in the La Blache sector began in the 1950's with the discovery of iron and titanium 
mineralization. 
 
In 1951, the first titaniferous magnetite outcrops were discovered in anorthosite of Schmoo Lake 
(GM02209-A) by Anglo-Canadian Pulp and Paper Mills, which eventually became Bersimis Mining. 
From 1951 to 1954, Bersimis Mining conducted aeromagnetic and "dip-needle surveys" geological 
mapping, surface sampling, assaying and metallurgical test work (GM02209-B and GM02671). A 
total of 4 mineralized lenses were uncovered over a distance of 15 kilometres: Hervieux-West, 
Hervieux-East, Schmoo Lake and La Blache East (GM06409) (Figure 7-2). 
 
In 1954, three claim blocks held by the Bersimis Mining were visited by the MRNFQ (GM03107). 
The MRNFQ published a report and map jointly with Bersimis Mining that located and described 
the Hervieux-Est and Hervieux-Ouest occurrences (RP374) revealing the presence of medium to 
coarse grained magnetite in anorthosite. According to estimates made by Bersimis Mining at the 
time "these deposits contained 135,000,000 tons of mineral resources up to a depth of 300 feet. It 
was reported that the average content of the mineral resources was of 49% Fe and 21 % TiO2. This 
NI 43-101 non compliant historical mineral Resources and mineral reserve estimate was not verified 
by a qualified person and no sufficient work was done to classify the historical estimate as current 
mineral resources. It should only be considered has an indication of the iron-titanium mineral 
potential and not necessarily indicative of the mineralization of the La Blache property. 
 
A ground magnetic survey was completed by Prospecting Geophysics in 1959 (GM08681). Bersimis 
Mining completed 20 drill holes in 1964 (GM15462, GM15667 and GM15992) intersecting 
significant iron and titanium (more than 45% Fe and 15% TiO2.). The MRNFQ examined 
approximately 300 m of drill core sampling holes 4, 7, 8, 10, 11, 13 and 17 as well as two outcrops 
for petrographic and chemical analysis. Three lenses were identified and were apparently aligned 
over a distance of 6 km. The lenses vary from 100 m to 1,130 m in length and 45 m to 215 m in 
width (RG2002-01 and GM37408). Geochemical analysis tend to be consistent from one lens to the 
other (GM37408) averaging 50.4% Fe, 20.1% TiO2, 0.36% V2O5, 0.70% SiO2, 7.41% Al2O3, 1.26% 
CaO, 4.05% MgO, 0.19% Cr, 0.03% P and 0.02% S.  
 
The Mineral Resources Estimate reported by Bersimis Mining in 1964 (GM37408) was 79 million 
tons grading 48% Fe, 20.5% TiO2, 0.19% Cr and 0.36% V2O5. This NI 43-101 non compliant 
historical mineral resources and mineral reserve estimate was not verified by a qualified person and 
no sufficient work was done to classify the historical estimate as current mineral resources. It should 
only be considered has an indication of the iron-titanium mineral potential and not necessarily 
indicative of the mineralization on the La Blache property.  
 
An aeromagnetic map (2083G) covering the La Blache property area was published in 1968 by the 
Geological Survey of Canada. 
 
The La Blache sector was mapped at a regional scale during the MRNFQ's Grenville Project in 
1968-1969 (DP127 and RG162) when the name of La Blache Anorthosite Pluton first appeared on 
published maps. A geotechnical site investigation was completed in 1969 by L. Kish who collected 
several mineralized samples (GM26833, DP127 and RG162) with the following results (RG162): 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 40 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

0.53% SiO2, 50.12% Fe, 20.84% TiO2 and 0.20% V at Hervieux-West; 0.91% SiO2, 49.74% Fe, 
19.35% TiO2 and 0.20% V at Schmoo Lake and 0.66% SiO2, 51.34% Fe, 20.09% TiO2 and 0.21% V 
at Hervieux East. 
 
A large exploration campaign, the Manic Project, was undertaken by SOQUEM in 1976 covering 
34,700 km2 (GM49156, GM49162, GM49164 and GM49165) that included lake-bottom sediment 
geochemistry, airborne spectrometry and a geological survey. Following this campaign, SOQUEM 
outlined 66 areas of interest for base metals and other minerals without retaining the La Blache 
occurrence (DP86-18, MB86-58 and MB89-58). 
 
In 1980, three concession blocks totalling nine claims were staked by Les Ressources Camchib 
(GM37408) covering the Hervieux-West, Hervieux-East and Schmoo Lake occurrences. Camchib 
concluded that the titaniferous magnetite occurrences at La Blache represented an important source 
of titanium, iron and possibly of chrome and vanadium. 
 
In 1982, the three claim blocks were explored by Services Exploration (GM39253, GM39254, 
GM39255 and GM39256) who completed a geological and dip needle survey at Schmoo Lake 
without the discovery of any massive titaniferous magnetite. At Hervieux-Est, a geological survey 
uncovered 25 m to 30 m of massive magnetite. At Hervieux-West, ten samples of titaniferous 
magnetite contained between 49.20% and 50.58% Fe and between 18.40% and 21.86% TiO2. 
 
Metallurgical studies of the ilmenite mineralization were performed in 1992 (GM51848) at the 
Hervieux-Ouest occurrence as part of the concession then owned by Gaspésie Société d'Exploration 
Pétrolière et Minière. The testing was completed by BHP-UTAH and produced a heavy mineral 
concentrate of ilmenite containing 46% to 50% TiO2. In 1993, Gaspésie Société d'Exploration 
Pétrolière et Minière prospected the Hervieux East and West occurrences. The Hervieux East and 
West ilmenite occurrences contained 5% to 10% ilmenite, but was deemed uneconomic at the time 
and no further work was recommended. 
 
Lac La Blache was mapped in 2000 by the MRNFQ (RG2002-01). The La Blache anorthosite was 
represented on the new geological map (unit mPbla1) as well as the iron and titanium mineralization 
(mPbla5). 
 
A geological field excursion guidebook (MB2003-03) on the La Blache mineralization was published 
in 2003. 
 
In 2005, the MRNFQ (PRO2003-03) published new geochemical data of lake-bottom and stream 
sediments covering La Blache. Numeric data of airborne geophysical surveys were made available in 
2006 (DP2006-06). 
 
In 2006, Fancamp Exploration Ltd., performed metallurgical tests (GM62464) on two samples of 
titaniferous magnetite from the Hervieux-Est occurrence (GM62465). The two samples were 
analyzed by COREM contained in excess of 22% TiO2 and more than 67% of Fe2O3.

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

7. Geological Setting and Mineralization 

7.1 Regional Geology 

The La Blache property is located in the North Shore region of Quebec, part of the Grenville 
Geological Province (Figure 7-2). The Grenville extends for more than 2,000 km in length and skirts 
the North Shore of the St-Lawrence River. Its width varies from 300 km to 600 km and forms the 
south east segment of the Canadian Shield. The Archean rocks of the Superior Province and the 
Proterozoic rocks of the Otish Basin are separated from the Grenville Province by the Grenville 
Front. The tectonic fabric of the Grenville is predominantly northwest-southwest trending.  
 

 
 
Figure 7-1: Regional Geology Map of Quebec Showing the La Blache Area 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 42 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

7.2 Local Geology 

The Grenville consists of gneiss domes and basins with complex and irregular structural patterns, 
intrusive rocks of variable composition, from gabbros to alkaline rocks. The circular shaped 
Manicouagan Structure located in proximity to the La Blache property was reportedly created by a 
meteorite impact some 214 million years ago. 
 
The lithologies and mineralizations of the project are as follows: lithologies are divided into three 
major units: the gneissic and intrusive rocks of varied composition of the Hulot Complex, intrusive 
rocks that include the east-west trending La Blache Anorthosite Complex, and late crosscutting 
gabbronorites, gabbros, diabasic gabbros, mangerites, granites and pegmatites (RG2002-02). The La 
Blache Anorthosite Complex is an almost circular batholith of 35 km by 20 km (GM52690) within 
intrusive rocks that extends for 100 kilometres by up to 20 kilometres. The anorthosites are cut by 
granites and pegmatite varying from a few centimetres to several metres of multiple orientations. 
 
Four lenses of titaniferous magnetite (Hervieux-West, Hervieux-East, Schmoo Lake and East of La 
Blache) are present as tabular bodies that are aligned over a 17 kilometre long arc (RG2002-01) 
located at the center of the anorthosites. The lenses are almost parallel to the axis of the large 
antiform defined by the anorthosites that is slightly discordant with the lithologies. The geology is 
taken from descriptions contained in a number of geological company and government reports 
(GM02671, GM52690, RG162 and RG2002-01). Lithologies are all of igneous origin and are divided 
into anorthosites, garnet anorthosites, pegmatites, gabbroic anorthosite and titaniferous magnetites 
of the La Blache Anorthosite Complex. 
 

7.2.1 Anorthosites 
The anorthosites at the core of the La Blache Anorthosite Complex are composed of at least 90% 
andesine to labradorite plagioclase megacrysts with minor pyroxenes, titaniferous magnetite, 
ilmenite, garnet, biotite, olivine, pyrrhotite and chlorite. The anorthosites occupy 75% of the total 
surface of the property. It is massive, medium to coarse grained, equigranular and automorphic. It is 
also weakly deformed, unaltered, non-foliated, but occasionally cataclastic. The anorthosites are grey 
colour on fresh surfaces, and the labradorite is recognizable by its bluish tinge. The anorthosites are 
slightly magnetic. 
 

7.2.2 Garnetiferous Anorthosites 
Similar to typical anorthosites, but contains between 5% and 15% garnet, the garnets are 
agglomerated masses of 5 centimetres to 15 centimetres linked to magnetite and ilmenite. The unit is 
located in direct contact with the iron oxides and is up to 25 m wide. 
 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 43 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

 
Figure 7-2: Geology Map of the La Blache Area 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 44 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

7.2.3 Pegmatites 
Dykes and veins of pink pegmatites cut all other units. They are composed of quartz and potassic 
feldspar with minor biotite and magnetite. 
 

7.2.4 Gabbroic Anorthosites 
The gabbroic anorthosites are distinguished from anorthosites by its content of 5% to 25% of mafic 
minerals. Contacts are gradual between the two units. 
 

7.2.5 Titaniferous Magnetite 
The titaniferous magnetite is easily identifiable by its black colour with a bluish reflection in contrast 
to the grey anorthosite. It is massive and is in contact with anorthosites that also occur as enclaves in 
the oxides. The typical composition is 80% titaniferous magnetite, 10% spinel, 5% to 10% ilmenite, 
and 5% pyroxene and/or plagioclase. 
 
The dominant structure on the Property has a northwest orientation as per the general alignment of 
the La Blache Anorthosite Complex. 
 
 
 
  



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 45 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

8. Deposit Types  
The La Blache property is composed of geological units likely to contain significant iron, titanium 
and vanadium oxide mineralizations of igneous origin and of economic interest. 
 
The mineralization at the La Blache property is composed of veins, dykes, lenses and tubular bodies 
of massive titaniferous magnetite linked to anorthosites that are common to the Grenville 
Geological Province. The Magpie Deposit also located on the North Shore constitutes one of the 
largest titaniferous magnetite deposits with reserves in excess of 800 million tonnes grading 43% Fe, 
11% TiO2, 1.6% Cr and 0.20% V (Vallée and Raby, 1971). The historic mineral reserves are strictly 
historical in nature and are non-compliant to NI 43-101 Mineral Resource standards and should 
therefore not be relied upon. A Qualified Person has not done sufficient work to classify the 
historical resource as current NI 43-101 compliant Mineral Resources. There is no guarantee that 
any future exploration would upgrade the historical Mineral Resources into current Mineral 
Resources. The La Blache property location is shown in Figure 8-1 as DLBA. 
 

 
Source: Mineral Deposits of Canada, Regional Metallogeny, Prospective Metallogenic Settings of the 
Grenville Province, by Louise Corriveau, Serge Perreault1 and Anthony Davidson).   
Figure 8-1: Grenville Geological Province Anorthosites & Fe-Ti-V Deposits 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 46 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

 
The oxide mineralizations of the La Blache property is part of a widely distributed deposit-type 
which is typically associated in space and time with major igneous events.  
 
Major deposits of titano-magnetite are divided into a phosphorus-rich type (Sept-Îles) and 
phosphorus-poor type (La Blache and Magpie mineralizations). Both mineralizations are distinctive 
in that they show high concentrations of chrome, the presence of the mineral spinel which is a 
reflection of the high Al2O3 contents of the rocks and relatively low vanadium (from trace to 0.40% 
V2O5). 
 
Opinions vary on the geological origins of mineralization. One theory supports an origin by 
accumulation of dense crystals in a magma chamber through settling under the force of gravity 
(Pang et al. 2008), while a second favours crystallisation from an immiscible oxide-rich magma within 
the silicate magma intrusive sequence (Zhou et al. 2005). 
  



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 47 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

9. Exploration  
Nevado 2010-2011 diamond drilling campaign was preceded by prospecting and an airborne 
Magnetic and Electromagnetic geophysical survey that covered both La Blache #1 and #2 claim 
blocks. This early work confirmed not only the presence of several massive and disseminated oxide 
occurrences, but also their continuity and consistent Iron, Titanium and Vanadium grades across the 
entire length of the La Blache Anorthosite Complex. . The following section summarizes the work 
outlined in the report titled "Work Report, Fall 2010 and Winter 2011, La Blache project, La Blache 
#1 and #2 Claim Blocks" by Jean Lafleur, P. Geo., dated August 15, 2011. 
 

9.1 Prospecting Program (June 2010 to November 2011) 

In June 2010, Nevado initiated detailed prospecting, geological mapping and grab/channel sampling 
on La Blache #1 and #2 claim blocks to establish continuity and grades of the magnetite-ilmenite 
lenses. The first occurrence tested was Hervieux East Extension (Figure 9-1) which outcrops along a 
50 long ridge totally stripped of vegetation due to previous forest fires in the area. 
 
Grab samples taken from a known historical showing, the Hervieux East Extension Occurrence 
located on the La Blache #1 claim block, gave an average of 51.6% Fe2O3 (Iron oxide), 18.6% TiO2 
(Titanium oxide) and 0.068% V2O5 (Vanadium Pentoxide) (Table 9-1 and Figure 9-7 ; Nevado news 
release dated March 30, 2010).

inventoried, weighed and dried; crushed 70% to under 2 millimetres; riffled split with a 250 gram

Blache Anorthositic Complex (LABC). The LBAC extends 35 km in a northeast-southwest direction

unit 100 m to the north. The Hervieux East Extension occurs along the western portion of a 
kilometric magnetic high signature on the Project.

In November 2010, Nevado announced the discovery of several new massive magnetite ilmenite

part of a 45 km long corridor forming the perimeter of an 18 km by 10 km ellipse (Figure 9-4: ). The 
new lenses are:

Farrell-Taylor Showing (located at Km 3, moving clockwise)

The ellipse which hosts the massive oxides is termed the La Blache Ring of Iron-Titanium-
Vanadium (the "Ring") (Figure 9-4: ) Highlights from the Ring include: 
 
(1) The target Ring forms an 18 km by 10 km ellipse encompassing a number of massive magnetite-
ilmenite lenses within the La Blache Anorthositic Complex located 160 km to 180 km. 
 
(2) The Ring is located entirely within the La Blache #1 and #2 claim blocks of the La Blache 
property. 
 
(3) The Ring currently hosts 9 massive magnetite-ilmenite lenses of various lengths 2 of which are 
historical, discovered and explored in the 1950's and 1960's (Hervieux East and Hervieux West), and 
seven (7) are new discoveries made by Nevado in 2010 (Hervieux East Extension, Hervieux 
Extension North, Farrell-Taylor, Lac La Blache West, Leduc, Leduc-Farrell and E. Girard 
Occurrences) (Figure 9-4: ). 
 
(4) Assays clearly demonstrate the continuity of the magnetite-ilmenite mineralization along the 
established 45 km trend of the Ring and that assay grades are consistent across the full trend being 
in the +60% Fe2O3, 17% to 23% TiO2 and 0.10% V2O5. 
 

9.2 2010 Airborne Magnetic and Electromagnetic Geophysical Survey 

Nevado completed a 3,425 line-kilometre airborne geophysical (Magnetic and Electromagnetic) 
survey (the Survey) covering the La Blache #1 and #2 claim blocks. 
 
The Survey targeted :  (1) massive, decimetric magnetite-ilmenite lenses, such as the 150 metres long 
by 35 metres wide magnetite-ilmenite outcrop of the Hervieux East Extension, where surface 
channel samples yielded up to 12 metres of 62.8% Fe2O3 and 19.6% TiO2 and smaller individual 
channel samples averaged 59% Fe2O3, 18.6% TiO2 and 0.11 V2O5 in a range of 51.1% to 62.8% 
Fe2O3, 17.7% to 19.7% TiO2 and 0.05% to 0.16% V2O5 (refer to the Nevado news releases dated 
October 28, 2010).  (2) semi-massive to massive sulphides known to occur in gabbroic rocks 30 km 
east of the Hervieux East Extension the eastern portion of the Project, similar to the Outardes- 
Three and Four Occurrences (Ministère des Ressources Naturelles et de la Faune du Québec or 
MRNFQ Deposit Files 22K/03-2002), where historic work yielded up to 50% sulphides in breccias 
and veins/veinlets carrying up to 0.94% Nickel and 0.36% Copper and 1.28% Nickel and 1.38% 
Copper in grab sample (#3157; GM 56307). Prospectair Geosurveys Inc., of Gatineau (Quebec) ran 
the airborne geophysical survey using a Robinson R44 helicopter. Specifications of the geophysical 
equipment are as follows: 
 
Geometrics Cesium split-beam total field magnetic sensor installed in a bird with a sensitivity of 
0.001 nT, a sampling rate of 10 Hz and a resolution better than 0.01 nT per measurement. The 
sensor can tolerate gradients up to 10 000 nT/m, and operates in a range from 20 000 nT to 100 000 
nT. A 0.5 nT noise envelope shall not be exceeded over 500 m line-length without a reflight. The 
electromagnetic system is a ProspecTEM system (Figure 9-10: ), that includes a 3-KW generator in 
the transmitter, electrically isolated from the helicopter; alternating 2.75-ms half sine pulses with 
intervening off-times of 13.916 ms; 1,000 samples of transmitter current and response per half cycle 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 61 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

(60 Hz); orthogonal (z) component receiver in bird above transmitter; 10-Hz output rate of 10 on-
time and 30 off-time window (z) component. The helicopter uses an OmniStar differential GPS 
navigation system to provide real-time guidance for the pilot and to position data to an absolute 
accuracy of better than 5 m. The GPS time and positional information will be digitally recorded on 
the data acquisition system at a sample rate of 1 sec. The base-station consists of a GEM GSM-19 
Overhauser magnetometer; a computer workstation and a complement of spare parts and test 
equipment serve as the base station. The GSM-19 magnetometer has resolution of 0.01 nT, and 0.2 
nT accuracy over its operating range of 20,000- to 100,000 nT. The rate of data output is 1 Hz.  
 

 
 
Figure 9-10: Prospectair Geosurveys Inc., ProspecTEM System Configuration with 
Magnetometer 
 
The airborne magnetic survey outlined the perimeter of the La Blache Anorthosite Complex 
showing a pervasive magnetic high of the predominantly magnetic gabbroic rocks of the rim (Figure 
9-11: ). In addition, the central portion of the Complex tends to be magnetically lower with the 
exception of several punctual magnetic anomalies occurring as lines, and ellipse of various sizes 
generally linked to the massive oxide mineralization scattered along the main La Blache Ring. The 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 62 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

larger elliptical magnetic highs tend to be magnetic intrusions: those to the west are linked to mafic-
ultramafic intrusions, while the plug at the southwest corner of the Argex Mining claims on La 
Blache #2 claim block is a magnetic granite.

The Farrell-Taylor Occurrence is centered on a magnetic high at the east end of the La Blache #1 
claim block (Figure 9-12: ). The shape of the magnetic high anomaly with the presence of a strong 
magnetic low to the west-northwest indicated a shallow east-dipping massive and/or heavily 
disseminated oxides lens of significant dimension, some 2,000 m by 500 m by 200 m wide. The 
Farrell-Taylor Occurrence became the prime drilling target for the 2010-2011 exploration period.

Occurrence, where conductive horizons occur at the surface expressions of the massive 
mineralization at Schmoo Lake and the dyke-like outcrop of the actual showing some 3 km to the 
east.

10. Drilling  
In 2010, Nevado secured the mining rights and completed exploration work as well as 9,700 m of 
exploration diamond drilling totalling 32 diamond drill holes (DDH) targeting the main mineralized 
Farrell-Taylor magnetite-ilmenite deposit. In 2011, Nevado completed a total 36 DDH for a total of 
12,600 m mostly on the Farrell-Taylor (6,850 m) and Hervieux East Extension (1,800 m) within La 
Blache #1.  Nevado also drilled on the Leduc-Farrell (1,800 m), E. Girard Showing (234 m) and 
other occurrences (2,973 m) within La Blache #2 claim block.  
 
Farrell-Taylor is located along the eastern segment of an east-west 3.5 km long by 1 km wide dual 
geophysical anomaly with a magnetic low, conductive western portion and a magnetic high, non 
conductive eastern portion. The geophysical modeling suggested a shallow east dipping (10° to 20°) 
25 metres to 200 metres thick magnetic lens of massive, semi-massive and disseminated magnetite-
ilmenite mineralization, later confirmed by drilling. The thicker portions closest to surface were 
believed to extend for a lateral distance of at least 1.5 kilometres and were first drilled on a 200 
metre by 150 metre grid pattern. Farrell-Taylor occurs at km 3 (in a clockwise direction) of the Ring. 
The average true thickness of the mineralized intercepts from drill core is 85% to 95% of the 
reported length along the core.

The 2010 helicopter-supported drilling program consisted of 32 BTW-sized drill holes totalling 
9,618 metres at Farrell-Taylor (Figure 10-1).

and more disseminated oxides lenses are outlined in Table 10-2.

(1) Core lengths in metres of massive oxides. 
(2) V2O5 assay results reported here used the ME-MS81 preparation (Lithium Borate Fusion) and 
assay method. 
(3) Wider intervals include disseminated (>10%), veins and semi-massive oxide mineralizations 
surrounding the massive oxides. 
n/a – purposely drilled outside the limits of the known mineralization to define the oxide corridors 
or drilled above the oxides 
 
All released drill holes and field samples assay results from 2010 and 2011 have shown similar grades 
for the massive and semi-massive vein-type oxide Iron, Titanium and Vanadium over the entire 45 
km long La Blache Ring of Iron-Titanium-Vanadium out of which Nevado owns directly more than 
37 km. Grades in the massive oxides range in the 59% to 70% Fe2O3, 17% to 22% TiO2 and 0.05 to 
0.15% V2O5. The higher grades are situated in the more massive oxides that are surrounded by 
anorthosites containing 5% to 25% disseminated and vein-type oxides ranging from a few metres to 
more than 100 m in core length which gave lower grades in the ranges of 15% to 45% Fe2O3, 5% to 
15% TiO2 and 0.03% to 0.10% V2O5.  
 
Massive, semi-massive, vein-type and disseminated (>10%) oxide mineralizations were intersected in 
25 of 32 drill holes, while 7 drill holes were either drilled outside the zone on purpose to define the 
limits of the oxide corridors or were drilled too shallow and above the mineralization. 
 
Based on the drilling and the concurrent geophysical modelling, the massive and semi-massive vein-
type oxide mineralization presently extends 1.5 km in down-dip length, 350 m to 750 m across and 
now averages 115 m in vertical width based on drill core lengths representing a significant volume of 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 71 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

mineralized material which is visually distinct from the surrounding hard, less dense and white to 
mauve coloured host anorthosites, since they consist of softer, dense mixed magnetite-ilmenite 
having metallic brown and dark grey to black colours. The massive oxide mineralizations are 
believed to be part of a series of sub-vertical, inclined and sub-horizontal dykes, sills, veins, 
stockworks and disseminations emplaced along multi-kilometric circular and elliptical configurations 
within the 35 km by 12 km La Blache Anorthositic Complex, such as the Ring  . 
 

10.5 2011 Diamond Drilling 

In September 2011, Nevado initiated and completed a second helicopter-supported diamond drilling 
campaign at its wholly-owned La Blache Iron-Titanium-Vanadium Property. The drilling campaign 
totalled 12,603 metres in 36 drill holes covering 6 occurrences: Farrell-Taylor, Farrell-Mason, Leduc-
Farrell, Hervieux East Extension, E. Girard and La Blache West-N. Tarbouche occurrences (refer to 
Nevado's news releases dated September 26, 2011, and March 1, 2012). The Farrell-Taylor drilling 
from the La Blache #1 Claim Block comprised 6,848.2 metres in 13 holes with the data included in 
the current mineral resources estimates.  
 
Drilling on the other 5 occurrences from the La Blache #2 Claim Block consisted of 5,755.1 metres 
in 23 holes as outlined in the following Table 10-4. Some 806.5 m were drilled in 3 holes at La 
Blache West–Nabil Tarbouche; 2,167.8 metres in 6 holes at Farrell-Mason; 1,805.1 metres in 9 holes 
at Leduc-Farrell; 741.8 metres in 4 holes at Hervieux East Extension; and 234.0 metres in 1 hole at 
E. Girard.

11. Sample Preparation, Analysis and Security 
 
The core from diamond drill holes were transported by helicopter from the drill sites to the Nevado 
core logging facility located 25 km to the west of the Farrell-Taylor Showing. There, the geologists 
and technicians from PJLEXPL Inc., a full-service exploration contractor from Laval, Quebec, 
under the supervision of Jean Lafleur, M.Sc., P. Geo., La Blache Project Manager, logged, sampled, 
tagged and splitted the core in half of 0.25 m to 1.0 m lengths using a hydraulic splitter.  
 
The individual sampled intervals of half-split core were inserted in tagged plastic bags, sealed and 
placed in large nylon bags ready for shipment to the ALS Laboratory Group ALS-Chemex facility in 
Val-d'Or, Quebec. ALS Chemex is a fully accredited laboratory under ISO 9001 and ISO/IEC 
17025 standards. Blanks and duplicates were inserted in the sample stream on-site at every 20 core 
samples. 
 
The V results were obtained by the ME-ICP61V. The Fe2O3, TiO2 and other major elements were 
obtained by ME-ICP06 in 2010. The Fe2O3, TiO2 and other major elements were obtained by ME-
XRF06 in 2011. 
 
The analytical protocol used at ALS Chemex  were the ME-MS81 for Trace Elements (Ag, Ba, Ce, 
Co, Cr, Cs, Cu, Dy, Er, Eu, Ga, Gd, Hf, Ho, La, Lu, Mo, Nb, Nd, Ni, Pb, Pr, Rb, Sm, Sn, Sr, Ta, 
Tb, Th, Tl, Tm, U, V, W, Y, Yb, Zn and Zr);  ME-ICP06 for Major Elements as Oxides was 
retained for Fe2O3, TiO2, V2O5 in 2010 (Al2O3, BaO, CaO, Cr2O3, K2O, MgO, MnO, Na2O, P2O5, 
SiO2 and SrO); ME-XRF06 for Major Elements as Oxides was retained for Fe2O3, TiO2, V2O5 
staring in 2011. Additional assay results included: (Al2O3, BaO, CaO, Cr2O3, K2O, MgO, MnO, 
Na2O, P2O5, SiO2 and SrO); ME-ICP61V for the Trace Element Vanadium using the Aqua-Regia 
Total Digestion Method; OA-GRA05 for Loss on Ignition (LOI's) at 1,000°C; TOT-ICP06 for 
Total Calculations of Major Elements; and ME-MS61 for the Trace and Major Elements as Metals 
(Ag, Al, As, Ba, Be  Bi, Ca,  Cd, Co, Cr, Cu, Fe, Ga, K, La, Mg, Mn, Mo, Na, Ni, P, Pb, S, Sb, sc, Sr, 
Th, Ti, Tl, U, V, W, Zn.  
 

11.1 Sample Preparation and Analysis 

The core from diamond drill holes were transported by helicopter from the drill sites to the Nevado 
core logging facility located 25 km to the west of the Farrell-Taylor deposit. The handling and 
transportation of the drill core samples was conducted by employees or contractors of PJLEXPL 
Inc., a full-service exploration contractor from Laval, Quebec, under the supervision of Jean Lafleur, 
M.Sc., P. Geo., La Blache #1 and #2 Project Manager. Drill cores were logged, sampled, tagged and 
half-splitted in 0.25 m to 3.0 m lengths using a hydraulic splitter.  
  
From the beginning of exploration on the La Blache project by Nevado since 2011, the drill core 
samples were sent for analysis at ALS Minerals of Val-d'Or, Quebec, and/or Vancouver, British 
Columbia, Canada. 
 
All samples received at ALS Minerals were digitally inventoried using a bar-code and then weighed. 
Samples having excess humidity were dried. Sample material was crushed in a jaw and/or roll 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 77 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

crusher to 70% passing 9 mesh. The crushed material was splitted with a rifle splitter to obtain a 250 
g sub-sample which was then pulverised to 85% passing 200 mesh using a single component (flying 
disk) or a two component (ring and puck) ring mill.  
  

11.2 Quality Assurance and Quality Control Procedure 

In addition of the standard laboratory QA/QC programs, Nevado implemented its own internal 
QA/QC protocol consisting in the insertion of blanks and core duplicates in the Project sample 
series.  
 

11.2.1 Analytical Blanks 
Nevado implemented the insertion of analytical blanks in the sample series as part of their internal 
QA/QC protocol. The analytical blanks are made of sand from a nearby beach, approximately 10 
km from the Farrell-Taylor deposit. The blank samples are inserted at every 20 samples in the 
sample series. A total of 226 analytical blanks were analyzed by using the same analytical measures as 
described above corresponding to 2.4% of the samples analyzed during the 2011 exploration 
program. From the 226 blanks analyzed, 144 came from the FT-XX series belonging to the Farrell –
Taylor Deposit sector. All of the 226 blanks analyzed returned values over the method detection 
limit as well as 5 times and 10 times the detection limit. Figure 11-1 shows the various plots of the 
variation of the analytical blanks according to blank numbers (with time). The Table 11-1 shows the 
descriptive statistics of the blanks result during the 2011 drilling program. The average Fe2O3 grade 
is 3.78%, which is far below the 59.70% average (see section 14.5). The 0.51% TiO2 average is also 
far from the 18% TiO2 observed in the deposit (see section 14.5). The 0.0049% V average is also far 
from the 0.18% V observed in the deposit (see section 14.5). 
 
No significant changes or anomalous values for Fe2O3, TiO2 and V2O5 (V) were observed on the 
2011 blanks. However, as described in the Figure 11-1, some peeks of higher and lower values were 
observed.  The vanadium grades are more scattered than the other minerals however, there appears 
to be no significant contamination.

As part of the Company's QA/QC protocol, the remaining half core duplicates from 216 
mineralized core samples were sent for analysis to ALS Minerals. The analyzed samples were 
selected from the drill holes completed during the 2011 exploration program. For the 216 core 
duplicates analyzed 78% of the Fe2O3 assay pairs were reproduced within ±10% and 90% 
reproduced within ±20%;  60% of the TiO2 assay pairs were reproduced within ±10% and 79% 
reproduced within ±20%; 61% of the V assay pairs were reproduced within ±10% and 79% 
reproduced within ±20%. The sign test for the duplicates analyzed did not indicate any bias on the 
Fe2O3, V and TiO2 results (Table 11-2 and Figure 11-2).  
 
Although no analytical bias was observed, SGS Geostat recommends sending the core duplicates to 
a second certified laboratory in order to establish if there is a significant error from one laboratory to 
another. This suggestion is in line with the finding of the Data Verification section. The  Figure 11-2 
shows correlation plots of the analyzed remaining half core duplicates sent to ALS Minerals.

11.2.3 QA/QC Conclusions 
No significant changes or anomalous values for Fe2O3, TiO2 and V2O5 (V) were observed. The 
QA/QC results are considered to be adequate.  
 
216 half core duplicate samples were selected from the drill holes completed during the 2011 
exploration program. No analytical bias was observed. It is SGS Geostat's opinion that the QA/QC 
protocol and the insertion of control samples by Nevado are within industry standards. The data is 
of sufficient quality to support mineral resources estimation. 
 
Although there is no analytical bias encountered, SGS Geostat recommends sending the core 
duplicates to a second certified laboratory in order to establish if there is a significant error from one 
laboratory to another. This suggestion is in line with the finding of the Data Verification section.  
 
SGS Geostat also recommends sending sufficient material from the Farrell-Taylor or other known 
similar occurrences and showings to a certified laboratory in order to make certified reference 
material (standards).

12. Data Verification 
The digital drill hole database supplied by Nevado was validated for the following fields: collar 
location, azimuth, dip, hole length, survey data and analytical values. The validation did not return 
any significant issues. However, the collar coordinates present in the database were taken from a 
handheld GPS. As part of the data verification, the analytical data from the database has been 
validated with values reported in the laboratories analytical certificates. The total laboratory 
certificates verified amounts to approximately 5% of the overall laboratory certificates available for 
the Project. There were no errors or discrepancies noted during the validation. 
 
The final drill hole database includes 2010-2011 surface holes of the Farrell-Taylor deposit until hole 
FT-11-13. The database cut-off date is May 23, 2012.Table 12-1 summarizes the data contained in 
the final drill hole database used for the Mineral Resources Estimates. SGS Geostat is of the opinion 
that the final drill hole database is adequate to support the Mineral Resources Estimates.

12.1 Check Sampling of 2011 Assay Results by SGS Geostat 

SGS Geostat completed analytical checks of drill core duplicate samples taken from selected Nevado 
2011 diamond drill holes on the Farrell-Taylor deposit as part of the independent data verification 
program. SGS Geostat also conducted verification of the laboratories analytical certificates and 
validation of the Farrell-Taylor database supplied by Nevado for errors and discrepancies. 
 
During the March 26-27, 2012 site visit by the author, Maxime Dupéré P.Geo., a total of 95 
mineralized core duplicates from the Farrell-Taylor deposit were collected from holes FT-11-01 and 
FT-11-02 and submitted for analysis at SGS Minerals laboratory in Lakefield (SGS Lakefield), 
Ontario, Canada. The duplicate samples were processed using strong acid digestion plus fusion of 
acid and ICP-OES finish (SGS code ICP 46C) for V and Ti. The Borate fusion-XRF method (by X-
Ray Fluorescence spectrometry) (SGS code XRF46C) was used for Fe2O3, TiO2 and V2O5.  Two 
blanks were inserted respectively at the beginning and ending the sample series. One certified 
reference material was also inserted in the samples series (OREAS 65a). Figure 12-1 shows 
correlation plots for the duplicate data versus the original data. A summary of the statistical analysis 
conducted on the data is shown in Table 12-2:  
 
Overall the correlation of the Fe2O3 assay results shows a good relationship. No statistical bias was 
observed. Furthermore, 0.9% difference was observed on the average grades. On the other hand, 
SGS Geostat observed significant differences between TiO2 (2.2%) and V (7.9%) assay results.

12.1.1 Specific Gravity 
As part of the SGS Geostat independent check sampling program, specific gravity (SG) 
measurements was ordered on all of the same 95 mineralized core samples collected during the 
March 26-27, 2012, site visit from drill holes FT-11-01 and FT-11-02.  From these 95 samples, some 
51 were considered to be in the massive iron oxide layers and 44 in a mixed zone of iron oxides and 
anorthosite. The measurements were performed using the water displacement method (weight in 
air/volume of water displaced) on representative half core pieces (45 iron oxides samples) weighting 
between 2.03 kg and 6.92 kg in the massive iron oxides (mineralization) with an average of 5.67 kg. 
The results from the measurements reported an average SG value of 4.63 g/cm3.

13. Mineral Processing and Metallurgical Testing  
 
In 2011, Neomet Technologies Inc. ("Neomet") of Dorval, Quebec, completed a first stage of 
metallurgical testing on the Farrell-Taylor massive oxides mineralization. Neomet adapted their 
proprietary process for extraction of all valuable metals from the massive oxides mineralization.  
 
Preliminary metallurgical testing of the oxide mineralization by Neomet indicated 90% recovery of 
Iron and 95% recovery of Vanadium from the oxide mineralization into a final high-purity product. 
Neomet demonstrated that Titanium could be 100% recovered from the leach solution into a TiO2 
product suitable for further processing to pigment-grade TiO2. Ammonium metavanadate ("AMV"), 
the precursor to V2O5, was recovered from the leach solution at a purity of 99.9%. 
 
Nevado plans to use Neomet's unique proprietary acid recovery and regeneration process, which 
operates at a fraction of the cost compared with more conventional and energy-consuming 
technologies such as pyrohydrolysis, especially when the latter is coupled with solvent extraction for 
Iron and/or Titanium. Simultaneously, the Neomet process produces higher-grade ilmenite of 
greater than 99% purity (TiO2), which is a premium product suitable for the pigment market or for 
processing into higher-quality steels. 
 
Neomet Technologies Inc. (Neomet) has developed a proprietary chloride-based process for the 
recovery of titanium as titanium dioxide, (TiO2), vanadium as vanadium pentoxide (V2O5) and iron 
as hematite (Fe2O3) from ores containing some or all of these elements. 
 
 

13.1  Head Sample 

Core samples received from Nevado were crushed, ground and screened to 100% passing 100 mesh 
(150 µm).  Ground material was blended, rolled and split in order to generate a representative head 
sample for chemical analysis.  The analysis is shown in Table 13-1.

overall reaction and the kinetics of extraction.

13.3 Recovery of TiO2 from Leach Filtrate 

Preliminary tests were carried out on a composite filtrate from the miniplant leach circuit.  The feed 
solution contained 19.3 g/L Ti, 716 mg/L V and 115 g/L Fe, of which 71.5 g/L was present as 
ferrous iron. 
 
99.6% of the titanium in solution was recovered into a product containing only 1.5% Fe.  No 
vanadium was detected giving a product of 98.8% purity.  One of the most important aspects of the 
Neomet's process is that the high titanium purity was obtained directly from the leach solution by 
force hydrolysis, without the need for a complicated solvent extraction process as commonly 
proposed.

13.4 Conclusion of the Laboratory Leach Testing 

The preliminary laboratory development program has shown that a simple leaching and hydrolysis 
process can readily recover high grade TiO2 from Nevado la Blache mineralized material.  The 
process is simple and flexible.  High extractions of iron and vanadium were also achieved. 
 

13.5 Miniplant Testing 

Following the successful laboratory studies, the La Blache mineralized material was run through the 
Neomet's miniplant in order to demonstrate a successful transition from laboratory batch testing to 
continuous operation. 
 

13.5.1 Miniplant Head Sample 
Same material used for the batch tests was used for the miniplant run.  A more detailed chemical 
analysis was done and compared favorably with the sample used in the laboratory testing program.  
The chemical analysis for the miniplant run is shown in Table 13-4.  
 
Table 13-4: Chemical Analysis for the Miniplant Run 
 

 
 
 
Since total equal +99% there is very little silicate gangue associated with the mineralized material. 
 

13.5.2 Miniplant Neomet Process 
The Neomet miniplant process comprised the flowing steps: 
• Leaching circuit with hydrochloric acid to dissolve the titanium and vanadium;  
• Hydrolysis for the recovery of TiO2 from the leach filtrate;  
• Purification of TiO2;  
• Solvent extraction of vanadium 
• Acid regeneration and iron hydrolysis.

13.6 Recovery Method 

An eventual commercial mill will more than probably follow the Neomet's process model.  The 
circuit that has been modelled is based on the miniplant testwork and contains the following     
sections:  
• Leaching in strong hydrochloric acid to dissolve the mill feed 
• Precipitation and calcination of titanium dioxide 
• Vanadium extraction and recovery 
• Relevant solid-liquid separation and washing steps 
• Acid recovery via Neomet's novel hydrolysis technology

anticipated that when all the flowsheet adjustments be made, the metal percentage recovery will be

14. Mineral Resource Estimation 
This section reports the results of a Mineral Resources Estimates for the Farrell-Taylor deposit. The 
Mineral Resources Estimates herein was completed by SGS Geostat and was disclosed in the 
Company news release dated May 23, 2012.  
 
The mineral resources have been estimated by Maxime Dupéré, P.Geo., Geologist for SGS Geostat. 
Mr. Dupéré is a professional geologist registered with the Ordre des Géologues du Québec and has 
worked in exploration for gold and diamonds, silver, base metals and iron ore. The author has been 
involved in mineral resource estimation work on a continuous basis over different mineral deposits 
such as iron-titanium-vanadium deposits, since he joined SGS Canada Inc. in 2006. Mr. Dupéré is an 
independent Qualified Person as per section 1.4 of the NI 43-101 Standards of Disclosure for 
Mineral Projects with respect to the owner of the mineral titles included in the Project. 
 

14.1 Mineral Resources of the Farrell-Taylor Mineral Deposit 

SGS Geostat conducted the current Mineral Resources Estimates for the Farrell-Taylor deposit 
using the 2010-2011 diamond drill holes from Nevado. The database used to produce the Mineral 
Resource Estimate ("MRE") is derived from a total of 45 recent 2010-2011surface drill holes, and 
contains the collar, survey, lithologies, and analytical results. The database cut-off date is March 20, 
2012 (refer to section 12 and Table 12-1 for a summary information of the records contained in the 
final drill hole database). 
 
During the MRE process, different assumptions were made. These assumptions were used in order 
to calculate modelling cut-off grades and resources cut-off grades following the "reasonable 
prospect for economic extraction" stated by the NI 43-101 regulation. There was no Whittle 
optimised shell done over the Farrell-Taylor deposit. The MRE stated herein do not have 
demonstrated economic viability.  
 

14.1.1 Nevado Farrell-Taylor Deposit Database 
Most of the drill hole intervals defining the modelled mineralized solids have been sampled 
continuously. The sampling gaps in the mineralized intervals were considered having the average 
grade of the mineralized interval for the purpose of the block model interpolation process. There are 
a total of 1,097 assay intervals with an assigned Fe2O3, TiO2, V value reported in the database used 
for the current MRE. The grade distribution of the Fe2O3, TiO2, and V assay data is normal (for 
Fe2O3) with more than one grade population observed in the data. Table 14-1 summarizes the 
statistics of the Fe2O3, TiO2 and V assay results reported in the drill hole database. The Figure 14-1 
shows the histogram of the Fe2O3 assay data used in the resource estimation. Assays containing -1 
(for missing values) grade values were not considered in this histogram.

14.1.2 Specific Gravity (SG) 
An average specific gravity of 4.6 g/cm3 was used to calculate tonnage from the volumetric estimates 
of the block model. The average specific gravity is derived from the 183 specific gravity 
measurements taken from representative mineralized core samples from the 2010 and 2011 drilling 
period by the client.  
 
Additionally, SGS Geostat ordered specific gravity measurements from its independent check 
sampling program. The results from this program are similar to the SG mentioned above (refer to 
section 12.1.1). SGS Geostat recommends carrying additional work on SG determination in less 
mineralized areas and in waste.  
 

14.1.3 Geological Interpretation and Modeling 
Nevado interpreted the Farrell-Taylor geological model from 45 recent surface drill holes on 
sections matching several orientations (0°, 330°, 340° and 350°). The interpretation was based on 
the lithological records of the Fe2O3, TiO2, V2O5 grades database. The interpretation on sections was 
linked together into a 3D meshed solid by the client. SGS Geostat reviewed and validated the model 
and added some minor modifications. The 3D Solid covers over 1,150 m in length in an ENE 
direction with an average width of 470 m. The deposit widens at depth starting at 200 m wide to the 
WSW to approximately 715 m wide to the ENE. The deposit is shallow dipping at 20° towards the 
ENE and reaches a maximal depth of 600 m below surface. The average thickness is 50 m with a 
minimum of 15 m and a maximum of 85 m in the deeper portion of the deposit.  The bedrock-
overburden interface 3D surface was not used since there is insufficient data to support the creation 
of an overburden contact. Additionally, the 3D Solid was not modelled over the topographic 
surface. 

 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 95 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

 
 
Figure 14-4: Section 350 of the Farrell-Taylor Deposit 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 96 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

 
Figure 14-5: Section 45875mE of the Farrell-Taylor Deposit

14.1.4 Composites 
Block model grade interpolation was conducted on composited assay data. A composite length of 
1.5 m was selected to reflect the average assay interval length. Compositing is conducted from the 
start of each mineralized intercept (Fe2O3 mineralization) of drill holes. The last composite kept at 
the end of the mineralized intercept has a minimum length of 0.75 m. The selected length of the 
composites directly influences the amount of dilution of the model. The longer the composites are, 
the more likely they will be diluted. The selected length is considered suitable in comparison to the 
mean length of 1.29 m and the median length of 1.5 m of the assay lengths included in the 
mineralized intercepts as well as the dimension of the blocks used. Assay capping was not necessary. 
 
At total of 961 composites were generated. The modeled 3D wireframe envelope was used to 
constrain the grade composites. Table summarizes the statistics of the composite grade data.  
 
 
Table 14-2: Composites Summary Statistics 

 
 

14.1.5 Analysis of the Grade Distribution 
The Fe2O3 (%) grades of the composite samples show a distribution approaching the normal law 
with the presence of low and higher grade populations. In core samples, the maximum grade is 
70.97% while the minimum 2.65% Fe2O3 (refer to the histograms below). 
 
The TiO2 (%) grades of the composite samples show a distribution approaching the normal law with 
the presence of low and higher grade populations. In core samples, the maximum grade is 22.71% 
while the minimum grade is 0.26% TiO2 (refer to the histograms below). 
 
The V (ppm) grades of the composite samples show a distribution approaching the normal law with 
distinctive low and higher grade populations. In core samples, the maximum grade is 4,643.87 ppm 
and a minimum of 8.00 ppm (refer to the histograms below).

14.1.6 Resource Block Modeling 
A block size of 10 m (E-W) by 10 m (N-S) by 10 m (vertical) was selected for the resource block 
models based on drill hole spacing, width and geometry of the mineralization. The block model is 
constrained by the 3D wireframe solids of the massive iron oxide mineralization solid designed by 
Nevado.  The block model contains a total of 22,199 blocks.
