14.1.7 Grade Interpolation Methodology 
The grade interpolation for the block models was completed using Inverse Distance Squared 
Method (1/d2). Anisotropic search ellipsoids were selected for the grade interpolation process based 
on the analysis of the spatial continuity of composites using variography.  This method did not 
highlight sufficiently any preferred mineralization directions. The length of the ellipsoid was 
attributed according to the general shape of the KL1 solid.  
 
Limits were set for the minimum and maximum number of composites to be used for the 
interpolation and restrictions were applied on the number of composites used from each drill hole. 
The interpolation process for the high grade block model was conducted using 3 successive passes 
using the same search conditions from one pass to the next until all blocks were interpolated. The 
orientation of the search ellipsoid, which is identical for each interpolation pass, is N070° in 
azimuth, negative -20° dip and has a 0° spin. Table 14-4 describes the different ellipsoids used 
during the interpolation process. 
 
Table 14-4 : Search Ellipsoid Parametres 

 
 
 
In the first pass, the search ellipsoid dimension was 150 m (long axis) along strike, 150 m 
(intermediate axis) along dip and 15 m (short axis) perpendicular to the strike and dip. The shape of 
the ellipsoid corresponds to the general shape of the mineralized body. Search conditions required 
to estimate each block were defined by a minimum of 7 composites and a maximum of 20 
composites with a maximum of 3 composites selected from each drill hole. The first pass resulted in 
the interpolation of 45% of the blocks.  
 
In the second pass, the search ellipsoid dimension was increased to 300 m by 300 m by 30 m with a 
reduction of the anisotropy. The search conditions were the same as the first pass interpolation. The 
second pass resulted in the interpolation of 52% of the blocks. 
 
The third interpolation pass estimated the remaining blocks (3% of total). The ellipsoid dimension 
for the last pass was increased to 600 m by 600 m by 60 m with search conditions defined as a 30 
composite maximum and a 3 composite minimum with a maximum number of composites per drill 
hole set to 3 (refer to Figure 14-4 and Figure 14-5). Figure 14-9 shows blocks with TiO2 grade 
interpolation results for level Z at 250 m.  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 

Search Ellipse Avimuth Dip Spin Major Axis (m) Medium Axis (m) Minor Axis (m)
Pass 1 70 -20 0 150 150 15
Pass 2 70 -20 0 300 300 30
Pass 3 70 -20 0 600 600 60

There are no reserves reported here. The resources reported in this document are compliant with 
current standards as outlined in the National Instrument 43-101. During the MRE process, different 
assumptions were made. These assumptions were used in order to calculate modelling cut-off grades 
and resources cut-off grades following the "reasonable prospect for economic extraction" stated by 
the NI 43-101 regulation. 
 

14.2 Titanium Equivalent Grade in the Resource Estimation 

SGS Geostat introduced a Titanium Equivalent (TiO2Eq) calculated variable into the deposit 
estimation.  Mr. Mike Curtis of Nevado provided a price list of Vanadium, Iron and Titanium as of 
April 29, 2012 (Table 14-5). SGS Geostat did not do an extensive research of the dollar value of the 
vanadium, titanium and iron concentrates. A validation of the commodity prices was done from 
available public information and from available information from similar projects.

Titanium Equivalent Grade Equation:  
 
TiO2 Eq (%) = TiO2 + ((Fe2O3*0.62*120) / (1*2500)) + ((V*1.7852*0.0001*1*13500) / (1*2500)) 
TiO2 Eq (%) = TiO2 (%) + (V (ppm)*1.7852*0.0001*5.4) + (Fe2O3 (%)*0.033) 
 
Where V2O5 (%) = V (ppm)*1.7852*0.0001 
 
Prices were given by Mike Curtis of Nevado and the recoveries were taken from Neomet's 
proprietary confidential report. 
 

14.3 Cut-Off Grades (%) 

SGS Geostat used the Titanium equivalent grade for the definition of a cut-off grade (%) (COG). 
This equivalent grade can be defined as a temporary grade, which when used with TiO2 recovery and 
TiO2 price, gives the correct NSR for one tonne of ore. This grade equivalent combined TiO2 
recovery and TiO2 price can be used to calculate a marginal/processing cut-off grade for resource 
modeling purpose. The COG formula is defined as followed: 
 
COG (%)  = 
   RecoveryTiO2 (%) x PriceTiO2 (US$/t) 

(Processing & Mining costs (US$/t) + G/A costs (US$/t) 

 

SGS Geostat considered a Processing & Mining costs + G/A costs of $US 115/tonne and 
established the COG at 5.1% TiO2 Eq. From internal discussions with SGS Geostat mining 
engineers and Nevado, a mining and hydrometallurgical processing costs (including G/A) of $US 
115/tonne was retained.  The open pit method of extraction was considered and was estimated at 
$US 50/tonne ($US 100/tonne if waste material is included). A hydrometallurgical processing cost 
was estimated at $US 55/tonne and an extra $10/tonne was estimated for the G&A costs. 
Considering the local resources potential and availability of the nearby town of Baie-Comeau but 
also its relative short distance from smelters and larger mining agglomeration, SGS Geostat 
considers the mining and hydrometallurgical processing costs to be adequate.  
 

14.4 Mineral Resource Classification 

The MRC is in accordance with the specifications of the NI 43-101 Policy, namely in Measured, 
Indicated, and Inferred resources. Classification was done according to the density of drilling and 
level of confidence of the database information.  
 
Currently, there are no Measured and Indicated resources. Most of the sections contain drill hole 
information with average distance of more than 100 m between drill holes giving limited 
information on the deposit. There is insufficient information to build an overburden contact surface 
and the topographic surface does not fit the drill hole elevation coordinates. The fact also that the 
drill holes were geo-referenced only by a handheld GPS influenced the level of confidence in the 
database information. Lastly, the variogram built by SGS Geostat did not highlight clear and reliable 
correlations from the different directions on the deposit. 
  



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 104 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

SGS Geostat found a bias from its independent check sampling done on two 2011 drill holes 
mineralized intercepts (totalling 102 samples) during its site visit of March 26-27, 2012. The check 
samples were sent to the SGS Lakefield accredited laboratory in Lakefield, Ontario. A bias was 
identified on the Vanadium and Titanium values. An average difference of 7.9% and 2.2% in favor 
of the ALS Mineral laboratory respectively for V (%) and TiO2 (%) values. It is SGS Geostat 
opinion that this bias directly influences the level of confidence in the dataset and the classification 
of the Farrell-Taylor MRE.  
 

14.5 Classified Mineral Resources Estimate of the Farrell-Taylor Deposit  

The MRE of the Farrell-Taylor deposit has been estimated according to an open-pit mining 
perspective. The base case cut-off grade for the resources using a TiO2Eq COG of 5.1% is based on 
a Processing & Mining + G/A costs of $US 115/tonne.  The MRE reported here occurs within 
Nevado's La Blache property claim boundary. 

The MRE was estimated using analytical data from 45 recent surface drill holes. The analytical data 
was normalized to 1.5 m long composite. No capping was applied. The MRE was completed using a 
3D modelling and block model interpolation methodology. The interpolation was done by Inverse 
Distance Squared (1/d2) using three stages and search ellipsoids. The block model covers a strike 
length of 1,150 m and reaches a maximal depth of 600 m below surface. The average true thickness 
is 50 m with a minimum of 15 m and a maximum of 85 m in the deeper portion of the deposit. The 
block model was defined by block size of 10 m east-west, 10 m north-south and a 10 m elevation. 
An average Specific Gravity of 4.6 g/cm3 was used to calculate tonnage from the volumetric 
estimates of the block model.  

The MRE for the Farrell-Taylor deposit using a base case COG of 5.1 % TiO2Eq totals 101,700,000 
tonnes grading 59.7 % Fe2O3 (41.76 % Fe), 18% TiO2, 0.18% V (0.33 % V2O5) in the Inferred 
category. The following table summarizes the MRE of the Farrell-Taylor deposit with additional 
comparative cut-off grades.  A 6.7 % TiO2Eq equals to a Processing & Mining + G/A cost of $US 
150/tonne; whereas a 18.6 % TiO2Eq equals to a Processing & Mining + G/A cost of $US 
420/tonne.  
  



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 105 

SGS Canada Inc.

A limited sensitivity analysis (Table 14-7) was conducted using different bench intervals. Sensitivities 
analysis using the 5.1 % TiO2 Eq COG in 200 m bench sizes outlined that 89% of the mineral 
resources were above 300m depth. The author did not use any optimised shell. Mineral Resources 
which are not Mineral Reserves do not have demonstrated economic viability.

15. Adjacent Properties  
The information below was summarised from a NI 43-101 Technical Report under Argex Mining 
Inc. ("Argex"), titled: NI 43-101 Technical Report, PEA on the La Blache Fe-Ti-V Project, dated 
October 12, 2011. 
  
The Argex Property consists of one claim block covering 4,035.28 hectares or 40.35 km2, which 
surrounds Nevado's La Blache #1 claim block and is in turn surrounded by Nevado's La Blache #2 
claim block (Figure 4-3 to Figure 4-5). 
 
Titaniferous magnetite from the La Blache Property is hosted in 3 lenses: Hervieux-Ouest, 
Hervieux-Est and Schmoo Lake. A fourth lens (La Blache East) located in the extension of the three 
other lenses east of La Blache is not included since it lies outside the Property boundaries. The three 
lenses are aligned over a distance of 6 km. The lenses vary from 100 m to 1,130 m in length and 45 
m to 215 m in width (RG2002-01 and GM37408). Geochemical analyses tend to be consistent from 
one lens to the next (GM37408), averaging 50.4% Fe, 20.1% TiO2, 0.36% V2O5, 0.70% SiO2, 7.41% 
Al2O3, 1.26% CaO, 4.05% MgO, 0.19% Cr, 0.03% P and 0.02% S. 
 
Argex's La Blache Property holds mineral resources at Hervieux Est and Hervieux Ouest. The in-pit 
mineral resources calculated by the engineering firm BBA Inc., using a 11.76% Ti-equivalent cut-off 
grade, total 7.8 million tonnes grading 10.69% Ti, 41.92% Fe and 0.24% V in the Measured category, 
16.9 million tonnes grading 10.69% Ti, 41.95% Fe and 0.24% V in the Indicated category, and an 
additional 4.7 million tonnes grading 10.67% Ti, 41.76% and 0.25% V in the Inferred category. The 
compliant mineral resources estimate was completed by Met-Chem Inc., and reported in an Argex 
news release dated May 18, 2011.  
 
Argex has completed metallurgical test work consisting of preliminary leach testing using Process 
Research Ortech, whereby the leaching technology demonstrated high extraction efficiencies for the 
iron (greater than 90%), titanium (greater than 85%), vanadium (greater than 90%) and chromium 
(greater than 90%). In further testing, Process Research Ortech made two composite samples from 
drill core samples that Argex had previously analyzed at ALS-Chemex. The two composites (of 
approximately 100 kg each) were made from samples containing the lowest amount of iron 
(approximately 41% Fe expected) and the highest amount of iron (approximately 47% Fe expected). 
Initial test work has focussed on the processing of the high iron composite.  
 
The Argex PEA conceptual mine plan was developed using only open-pit methods. Mining would 
be at an average rate of 1.06 Mtpy over a 25-year or more mine life.  
 
The Qualified Person and author of this section was unable to verify any of the information 
provided under this section. The information and analytical results published by Argex are not 
necessarily indicative of the mineralization on Nevado's La Blache property that is the subject of this 
Technical Report.   



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 108 

SGS Canada Inc.

17. Interpretation and Conclusions 
The MRE reported in this document is compliant with standards as outlined in the NI 43-101 
regulations. This MRE was calculated using a minimum cut-off grade of 5.1% TiO2Eq and is 
amounting to 101,700,000 tonnes in the Inferred category at 59.70% Fe2O3, 41.76% Fe, 18.00% 
TiO2, 0.18% V and 21.75% V2O5Eq.  
  
The Farrell-Taylor deposit contains enough resources to justify additional work on the La Blache 
property that could lead to a preliminary economic assessment study. 
 
The independent sampling done by SGS Geostat revealed that the average grade of original assays 
for V (V2O5) is 7% higher than the independent samples. It shows a bias at a 95% confidence level 
for V (V2O5). SGS Geostat recommends sending duplicate samples to two different laboratories in 
order to determine correction factors. SGS Geostat recommends also continuing the QA/QC 
protocols. 
 
The La Blache property needs more definition diamond drilling before being ready for a mining 
operation which can be realized from the surface.  
  



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 110 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

18. Recommendations  
SGS Geostat recommends the continuation of detailed mapping-sampling and prospecting of 
known and potential mineralized oxides occurrences throughout the La Blache property.  
  
SGS Geostat also recommends additional drilling to significantly increase the quality of the 
geological information as well as the overall mineral resources and the geological model. With 
additional drilling and the revision of the geological model, an updated MRE could include 
Measured and Indicated resources categories.  
 
SGS Geostat recommends a continuation of drilling of the Farrell-Taylor deposit at an estimated 
cost of $C 3,191,000.  
 
The following budget recommendation (Table 18-1) is purely conceptual and does not include 
accommodations, meals, transportation and equipment rental costs.

SGS Geostat recommends implementing downhole survey measurements on relevant 2010-2011 
drill holes and on all of its future drilling. This includes dip, direction of surveyed holes. This will 
permit a more precise view of the present and future geological models.  
 



Technical Report, Resource Estimation, Farrell-Taylor deposit, La Blache Project Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada  Page 111 

SGS Canada Inc. 
 

SGS Geostat recommends implementing core orientation surveys on all selected future drilling. This 
includes dip, direction of geological and structural features. This will permit a more precise view of 
the geological features and structures shaping and affecting the mineral deposit.  
 
Although there is no analytical bias encountered on the Nevado duplicate core analysis (refer to 
Section 11.2.2), SGS Geostat recommends sending the core duplicates to a second certified 
laboratory in order to establish if there is a significant error from one laboratory to another. This 
suggestion is in line with the finding of the Data Verification section. The 7.9% difference for V and 
the 2.2% difference for TiO2 between original (ALS) and check samples (SGS Lakefield) results for 
V may be considered acceptable; however SGS Geostat strongly recommends addressing the matter 
by sending duplicate samples to two different laboratories in order to determine the bias. SGS 
Geostat also recommends continuing the QA/QC protocol by adding reference materials 
(standards) that match the general composition of the mineral deposits of the area. The author 
recommends sending sufficient material from the Farrell-Taylor deposit or other known similar 
occurrences and showings to a certified laboratory in order to produce and certify sufficient material 
for the standards. 
 
Additionally, SGS Geostat recommends sending reference materials (standards) to the same two 
different laboratories for the verification/evaluation of these results and to have a better 
understanding of the bias observed for V and TiO2. 
 
Finally, SGS Geostat recommends to fine tune the Neomet Process.

To accompany the Report entitled: "NI 43-101 Technical Report, Resource Estimation of the La Blache Project, 
Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada for Nevado Resources Corporation" dated May 14th, 2012. 
I, Maxime Dupéré, P. Geo, do hereby certify that:  

1. I reside 9660, Rue de la Chouette, Mirabel, Québec, Canada, J7N 0C9. 
2. I am a graduate from the Université de Montréal, Quebec in 1999 with a B.Sc. in geology and I have practiced 

my profession continuously since 2001. 
3. I am a registered member of the Ordre des Géologues du Québec (#501), and I am currently employed as a 

geologist by SGS – Geostat since May 2006. 
4. I have 11 years of experience in mining exploration in diamonds, gold, silver, base metals, and Iron Ore. I 

worked on several resources estimation technical reports and I have prepared and made several mineral 
resource estimations for different exploration projects at different stages of exploration. I am aware of the 
different methods of estimation and the geostatistics applied to metallic and non-metallic projects as well as 
industrial mineral projects. 

5. I am responsible for the preparation with exception of section 13 of this report entitled "NI 43-101 Technical 
Report, Resource Estimation of the La Blache Project, Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada for Nevado 
Resources Corporation" dated May 14th, 2012. 

6. I visited the site on March 26 and 27, 2012, I do not have previous involvements with Nevado Resources 
Corporation. 

7. Neither I, nor any affiliated entity of mine, is at present, under an agreement, arrangement or understanding or 
expects to become, an insider, associate, affiliated entity or employee of Nevado resources Corporation, or any 
associated or affiliated entities. I am an independent qualified person as described in section 1.5 of NI-43-101. 

8. Neither I, nor any affiliated entity of mine, own directly or indirectly, nor expect to receive, any interest in the 
properties or securities of Nevado resources Corporation, or any associated or affiliated companies.  

9. I have read NI 43-101 and Form 43-101F1 and have prepared this report entitled "NI 43-101 Technical 
Report, Resource Estimation of the La Blache Project, Côte-Nord, Québec, Canada for Nevado 
Resources Corporation" dated May 14th, 2012 in compliance with NI 43-101 and Form 43-101F1. 

10. To the best of my knowledge, information and belief, and, as of the date of this certificate, this technical report 
contains all scientific and technical information that is required to be disclosed to make this section of the 
technical not misleading.
